[2025-11-17T01:46:59Z] Akshay: X is a kind of household ghost or spirit in German folklore. X often help with household chores in return for gifts, and can be bribed into good behavior with gifts and offerings of food, such as milk. However, they can be playful and mischievous as well, and some X are actively sinister. X can respond with often gruesome reprisals if insulted or treated shabbily. ↵ X is also used to refer to spirits found in mines and underground shafts, which is also the etymology for the transition metal element Y. Y likely originated from frustrated German silver miners who would often encounter far less valuable and often toxic Y ore, attributing its presence to the trickery of X spirits who stole the silver and left Y in its stead. Give X and Y.

[2025-11-17T04:46:30Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: 10: This sentiment has been expressed throughout history, and Roman author Pliny the Elder alluded to the phrase about 2,000 years ago. The specific three-word phrase was coined by Desiderius Erasmus of Rotterdam. The phrase refers to the tendency of people to be forthright and candid with information in a specific situation. Greek historian Heredotus wrote that if the Persians decided something under that situation, they would reconsider it after that situation no longer applied. Later Greek authors added that if the Persians decided something when that specific situation did not apply, they would reconsider it when it did apply again. Funda is enough, bonus for exact three-word phrase.

[2025-11-17T05:40:44Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Q. The Erdős number describes the "collaborative distance" between mathematician Paul Erdős and another person, as measured by authorship of mathematical papers. A number of variations on the concept have been proposed to apply to other fields, notably the Bacon number, connecting actors to the actor Kevin Bacon by a chain of joint appearances in films. A small number of people are connected to both Erdős and Bacon and thus have an Erdős–Bacon number, which combines the two numbers by taking their sum. ↵ Even further extension has been made possible. For example, the "Erdős–Bacon–X number" is the sum of the Erdős–Bacon number and the collaborative distance to X in terms of singing in public. ↵ Stephen Hawking’s score is 8. Natalie Portman is 11. Id X.

The 1828 Presidential Election in America was hotly contested by John Quincy Adams and Andrew Jackson, representing parties that were both new organizations. For Jackson’s opponents, letting the public rule was akin to being under the governance of mindless beasts and Jackson himself was also labelled with a similar insulting epithet.  Instead of refuting the accusation, Andrew Jackson shrewdly embraced it, converting into a symbolism of persistence, loyalty, humility and an unfailing ability to carry responsibility.   Furthermore, during his term as president, Jackson refused to re-charter the National Bank, and newspapers of the day lampooned him by characterizing his stubbornness in classic cartoon fashion. [2025-11-17T19:37:07Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Q7. A common phrase, ___ _____ _____ ___ traces back to William Caxton, an English printer who, in 1484, was the first to publish a translation of Aesop's Fables in English. The moral of one of the stories, as translated, was "He that hath ben ones begyled by somme other ought to kepe hym wel fro(m) the same".  The fable itself is about a wolf who threatens to eat a dog. The dog tells him to wait and the dumb wolf lets the dog go. When wolf returns he can't get at the dog to eat the dog, and the dog says something along the lines of the phrase given by Caxton. Caxton's phrase has been rephrased plenty of times over the years until it evolved into the current phrasing in the 20th century.  FITB

[2025-11-17T19:49:49Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Q9. Nowadays the term X is colloquially a sporting term, although it was originally a word used in photography to denote either flimsy paper photo strips or tiny single images. An X camera was one with a sliding frame that jumped back and forth and allowed photographers quickly and easily to take multiple images on a single plate with their number, spacing, and placement controlled by detachable rods. This motion of the cameras may have been what inspired its modern usage.  Much like the word X itself, X photos were fun; mostly of subjects goofing around, interacting with a conventionalized set of props, experimenting with moods and identities and costumes or simply reveling in the sheer fun of having their pictures taken. ID X.

The aim of X cabinets is to stop unauthorized people drinking the contents (in particular, "servants and younger sons getting at the whisky"), while still allowing them to be on show.
